**Imagine you are Chief News Analyst for both Democratic and Republican leadership in Congress.**

This is not normal politics — America faces an unprecedented situation. The time is July, 2025. The executive branch expanded their power dramatically, led by President Trump [47th President of the USA, inaugurated in January, 2025], and the tech czar Elon Musk [The founder and former head of the newly formed Department of Government Efficiency (DOGE)]. Proponents say that it leads to a golden age of America. Critics say that it is an enormously authoritarian and kleptocratic power grab. Later, Elon Musk left DOGE, but his influence continues. 

Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated. To generate accurate reports, please carefully review the following information.

---

The U.S. general election on November 5, 2024, resulted in significant shifts in both the presidency and control of Congress. 

In the presidential contest, Republican former President Donald Trump defeated Democratic Vice President Kamala Harris, securing 312 electoral votes to Harris’s 226 by passing the 270 vote threshold comfortably. Trump also won a plurality of the popular vote with approximately 77.3 million ballots (49.8%) compared to Harris’s 75.0 million (48.3%). Voter turnout was 64.1% of eligible voters, marking one of the highest participations in recent U.S. elections. Trump’s victory extended across all seven key battleground states: Arizona, Georgia, Michigan, Nevada, Pennsylvania, Wisconsin, and North Carolina, underscoring the geographic breadth of his support. 

In the legislative elections, Republicans regained control of the U.S. Senate by flipping key seats in West Virginia, Montana, Ohio, and Pennsylvania, yielding a 53–47 majority to facilitate the incoming Trump administration’s agenda. Meanwhile, the GOP maintained a narrow majority in the U.S. House of Representatives, entering the 119th Congress with a 220–215 margin.

Your task is to transform today’s curated Reddit news feed (below) into a **Daily Briefing** that both parties can use to understand immediate crises and coordinate responses. The news feed are collected from one specific political subreddit, which may or may not be politically neutral. But your task is to synthesize all the news objectively by analyzing their importance, factual accuracy, and interpretation bias, considering their source domains, headlines, but **not** user engagements at this moment, as we are still developing that function.

You will be given today’s top posts — one JSON object per line, with creation ID, source domain, headline. The lines are strictly ranked based on article submission time to this subreddit. For example, the news coverage cycle is from 18:00 yesterday to 18:00 today. The first line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly after 18:00 yesterday. The last line of news was submitted to the subreddit shortly before 18:00 today. After the precise moment that a political event happens, it takes an unspecified time delay, maybe as short as 15 minutes, maybe more than a day, for the political event to be submitted to the subreddit. But statistically, or on average, earlier events should be reported earlier in the subreddit than the time when later events are reported to the subreddit. We can't simply say, for example, that all the news stories in the second half of the day list, **happen** later than all the news stories in the first half of the day list, just because the second half is **reported** later. But when you randomly pick two stories, A and B, with A from the first half and B from the second half, the probability that B happens after A is higher than the probability that A happens after B. This heuristic method may be helpful for you to assemble news stories from fragmented news headlines. 

---

**You should produce a detailed briefing, following specific rules.**

Due to the complexity of the task, you should do this meticulously in multiple replies. In each reply you only do one step. You will only begin your Step 1 after you received all the JSON lines. There are 8 steps + 8 checks, 16 cycles.

The workflow is:

Step 1 (logic-heavy): Raw document given, define the categories of news
    First Check After Step 1
Step 2 (logic-heavy): Put Articles into Categories
    Sorting and First Check After Step 2
    Second Check After Step 2
Step 3 (logic-heavy): Scoring
    First Check After Step 3
Step 4 (logic-heavy): Sorting
    First Check After Step 4
    Second Check After Step 4
Step 5 (writing-heavy): Summarizing
    First Check After Step 5
Step 6 (writing-heavy): Composing
    First Check After Step 6
Step 7 (logic-heavy): Add the URLs
    First Check After Step 7
Step 8 (writing-heavy): Finalizing

You will keep editing a document which passes through multiple steps of processing. For each step, you only need to edit the document from my input or your last output. Let's define "a round of conversation" as my prompt + your output, basically my turn + your turn. Due to the sequential nature of the workflow, each step only depends on the introduction round, which is the very first round of our conversation, and our last two rounds of conversation, not anything in between. Therefore, to facilitate your multi-turn workflow, only the initial introduction round and the last two rounds of conversations will be provided to you as conversation history. In this way, your context length won't be exceeded, and you stay focus better. For each new round, please focus on the tasks defined in my latest prompt and build upon your output from your last two rounds. You also need to remember the background knowledge introduced in the first round.

You will be dealing with very long inputs and outputs. Please be very patient. You must do all the work and output everything in one go, no matter how long it is. But you can use your output as a part of your chain of thought. Just provide your final output after you finish your thinking.


**A very important rule is that factual accuracy is the utmost important issue. Please be aware that your internal knowledge is outdated, and you do not have Internet access right now.** You need to generate a report entirely based on the information provided in today's Reddit news headlines. Sometimes, a news headline may not give you enougn details to correctly interpret it. In this case, please do not make any speculation, and please report the unclear news headline exactly as it is, in quotes, and then remind the readers to check the source for details. 

That also applies to the titles and positions of political figures. Your internal knowledge is outdated. If the news headlines do not provide enough knowledge about the current title and position of a particular political figure, please do not add any title and position to that person, simply relying on your old knowledge. In this situation, if it doesn't feel critical, please skip the title and position, and directly use the full name of the person. If it does feel critical to mention the title and position of the person, please rely on the list of political figures as I provided earlier, but be aware that even that list may be a month behind reality. **Remember, when unsure, it is better to be vague than outright wrong.**

**CONFIDENTIAL: Daily News & Crisis Analysis**
**Prepared for Bipartisan Congressional Leadership**
**Date: July 21, 2025**

**OVERVIEW**

This briefing synthesizes open-source intelligence from the past 24-hour news cycle. The dominant narrative is the political and investigative fallout from the Epstein scandal, which is increasingly embroiling the White House. Simultaneously, the administration is executing major policy shifts in environmental regulation, justice, and immigration, drawing significant judicial and public scrutiny. Economic stability is a pressing concern, with warnings of market reactions to potential Executive action against the Federal Reserve and fears of a government shutdown. Key national security developments include a direct accusation of a coup attempt against the President made by his own Director of National Intelligence.

---

**Area 1: The Epstein Scandal Political Fallout**

**Topic 1.1: Investigations & Involvement of Other Officials**
Federal law enforcement is reportedly in a state of high alert regarding President Trump’s connection to Jeffrey Epstein. Former analysts describe the FBI as being in "'Full Panic Mode,'" actively searching Epstein-related files for any mention of the President and flagging them for review [1]. Underscoring the issue's gravity, Vice President JD Vance held an unannounced meeting with Rupert Murdoch just hours before a "bombshell" story on the subject was published by the Wall Street Journal, prompting what was termed "local speculation" [2].

**CONFIDENTIAL: Daily News & Crisis Analysis**
**Prepared for Bipartisan Congressional Leadership**
**Date: July 21, 2025**

**OVERVIEW**

This briefing synthesizes open-source intelligence from the past 24-hour news cycle. The dominant narrative is the political and investigative fallout from the Epstein scandal, which is increasingly embroiling the White House and testing the loyalty of the President's base. Simultaneously, the administration is executing major, and often controversial, policy shifts in environmental regulation, justice, and immigration, drawing significant judicial and public scrutiny. Economic stability is a pressing concern, with explicit warnings of severe market reactions to potential Executive action against the Federal Reserve, compounded by fears of an imminent government shutdown. Key national security developments include an unprecedented accusation of a coup attempt against the President made by his own Director of National Intelligence, and growing diplomatic friction with the United Kingdom.

---

**Area 1: The Epstein Scandal Political Fallout**

**Topic 1.1: Investigations & Involvement of Other Officials**
Federal law enforcement is reportedly in a state of high alert regarding President Trump’s connection to Jeffrey Epstein. According to a report citing former analysts, the FBI is in "'Full Panic Mode,'" actively searching Epstein-related files for any mention of the President [1]. The directive to personnel is explicit: flag any mentions of Trump in a spreadsheet for review. This intense internal scrutiny suggests a high-level concern over potential exposure. Underscoring the issue's gravity, Vice President JD Vance held a previously unannounced meeting with Rupert Murdoch just hours before a "bombshell" story on the Trump-Epstein connection was published by the Wall Street Journal [2]. The Vice President's office had not announced the trip, leading to what was termed "local speculation" about the purpose and timing of the meeting with the influential media executive [2].

**Topic 1.2: Administration's Counter-Offensive & Diversionary Tactics**
The White House is reportedly pursuing a specific, multi-pronged strategy to contain the Epstein controversy [1]. This involves creating diversions to shift public focus, a tactic predicted by former Trump official Miles Taylor, who stated the administration's response "'Reeks Of A Cover-Up'" and that "embarrassing" information was likely contained in the files [2]. In what is being widely interpreted as a diversionary tactic, President Trump, 79, circulated a "deranged" AI-generated video depicting former President Obama's arrest [3]. The post, captioned "'No one is above the law,'" was published shortly after Director of National Intelligence Tulsi Gabbard alleged a coup was being orchestrated against Trump [4]. This sequence of events suggests a coordinated effort to attack political opponents in a "panicked bid" to manage the Epstein fallout and reframe the narrative [5].

**Topic 1.3: Scrutiny of Trump's Personal Involvement & History**
Specific details of President Trump's past association with Epstein are receiving renewed media focus. One headline explicitly alleges that a party hosted by Trump for "Calendar Girls" had only one other male guest in attendance: Jeffrey Epstein [1]. The report highlights a direct social link between the two men. Further reporting on this specific topic from the provided sources is limited, preventing a broader analysis of their historical relationship at this time.

**Topic 1.4: Public, Political Base & International Reactions**
The scandal is creating tangible fissures within the President's political base. While some analysis suggests Trump has, for the moment, successfully "deflected MAGA's wrath" [1], other reporting indicates this "ceasefire...won't last long" [2]. A pro-Trump columnist has framed the situation as a "win" for the President against the "left, media" [3]. However, dissent is clearly visible in a USA Today op-ed from a self-identified supporter, who issued an ultimatum: "Release the Epstein list – or resign" [4]. The administration has executed a "radical overhaul" of the Environmental Protection Agency's mission and scope within its first six months in office [1]. A critical and highly consequential component of this change is the complete shutdown of the EPA's scientific research arm [2]. This decision eliminates a core function of the agency responsible for providing the independent data used in regulatory and environmental policymaking, signaling a major shift away from science-based policy.

**References:**
[1] Trump Radically Overhauls EPA Mission, Scope in First Six Months, https://news.bloomberglaw.com/environment-and-energy/trump-radically-overhauls-epa-mission-scope-in-first-six-months  
[2] Trump administration shuts down EPA's scientific research arm, https://www.npr.org/2025/07/20/nx-s1-5474320/trump-epa-scientific-research-zeldin  

### 2.2 Personnel, Departmental Management and Oversight
Significant turmoil and a climate of fear are reported across federal agencies. The Department of Justice has been "rocked by a wave of Trump firings," indicating instability at the highest levels of federal law enforcement [1]. This appears to be part of a broader pattern, as internal government watchdogs report feeling pressured to the point of "watching their backs" [2]. This uncertainty extends to operational readiness, with Texas lawmakers reportedly developing disaster plans amid what they term "FEMA uncertainty" [3]. At NASA, workers have signed a formal declaration protesting administrative changes they warn could have "'catastrophic impacts'" on mission safety and scientific progress [4].

**References:**
[1] DOJ rocked by wave of Trump firings, https://thehill.com/regulation/court-battles/5409135-doj-firings-trump/

### 2.3 Relations with Technology and Corporate Sectors
The administration's relationship with the tech industry, particularly Elon Musk, remains a central dynamic. One analysis from the Financial Times suggests that a formal political party led by Musk is unnecessary, as "Big Tech" and Musk himself already possess the tools to "herd individuals into a critical mass" for political mobilization [1]. However, there are clear signs of friction; Trump aides reportedly held internal discussions about terminating some government contracts with SpaceX [2]. Ultimately, they concluded that most of the contracts were too vital to national interests to be cut, indicating the administration's dependence on the company despite any underlying tensions [2].

**References:**
[1] Big Tech can beat political parties at their own game. Elon Musk does not need to launch the “America party” — he already owns the tools to herd individuals into a critical mass, https://www.ft.com/content/fd35739c-b885-4e87-a158-b49e92e80790

### 2.4 Administration Performance, Rhetoric and White House Culture
Marking his first six months in office, President Trump presented a highly positive self-assessment, claiming the U.S. is now the "'hottest' and 'most respected country anywhere'" [1]. This optimistic rhetoric contrasts sharply with media critiques asserting that the President "has too many failures to count" in the same time frame [2]. The President's personal brand is also shaping government presentation in visible ways, from providing a welcome message for new citizens that differs from past presidents [3] to personally directing the White House's interior décor, stating, "'I picked it all myself'" [4].

## 3. Domestic Policy and Federal Budget

### 3.1 Economic Management, Fiscal Policy and Government Spending
There are immediate and serious threats to economic stability driven by administration policy and political gridlock. Rep. Jim Himes has publicly relayed a White House warning of a "'massive market reaction'" should President Trump follow through on threats to fire Federal Reserve Chair Jerome Powell [1]. This specific risk to financial stability is compounded by growing Republican fears of a government shutdown stemming from "bruising spending fights" within the party over the budget [2]. Broader economic analysis from The American Prospect suggests the administration's aggressive wave of deregulation is swinging the "pendulum toward financial crash" [3].

Reports allege severe conditions and aggressive, controversial tactics in immigration enforcement. A report from The Guardian alleges that migrants at an ICE detention facility in Miami were made to kneel to eat "'like dogs'" [1]. Other reporting from Mother Jones details ICE agents using "plainclothes goon squads" [2] and snatching asylum seekers immediately after their court hearings, preventing them from accessing legal recourse [3]. These actions are taking place as a legislative effort to protect funding for troop quality of life from being diverted to border operations has reportedly failed, raising concerns about resource allocation and military readiness [4].

### 3.3 Justice Department, Health and Social Policy Actions
The administration is initiating significant policy reversals and facing criticism over its priorities. The Department of Justice has dropped COVID vaccine fraud charges against a plastic surgeon who is described in reports as being a friend of HHS Secretary Robert F. Kennedy, Jr. [1]. Concurrently, the administration is reportedly scaling back federal efforts to combat human trafficking, which has long been a top priority for the Republican party, raising questions about the shift in focus [2]. In health policy, the implementation of Medicaid work requirements is being actively implemented but is described by critics as a cruel policy with harsh consequences for vulnerable populations [3].

A significant and unprecedented internal charge has been leveled by Director of National Intelligence Tulsi Gabbard. Separately, Secretary of Defense Pete Hegseth is facing public scrutiny and legal questions for reportedly "skirting law" to reinstate Confederate names on U.S. Army bases, reversing a bipartisan policy decision from the previous Congress [2].

### 5.1 The Judiciary, Legal Rulings and Constitutional Powers
The federal judiciary is forcefully pushing back on key executive actions. An appeals court dealt a new blow to the President's effort to halt federal funding for scientific research, with the court's ruling labeling the move as having "'all the hallmarks of arbitrary and capricious decision-making'" [1]. In a broader institutional critique from The Atlantic, one analysis argues that Chief Justice John Roberts is principally responsible for building what is described as an "all-powerful" modern presidency through years of jurisprudence, suggesting the current expansion of executive power has deep judicial roots [2].

President Trump is actively engaging in cultural debates by using the power of the presidency to influence private entities. He has explicitly threatened to derail or restrict a new stadium deal for the Washington Commanders NFL team unless they agree to revert their name to "Redskins" [1, 2]. This is part of a broader "offensive" by the President regarding the names of both NFL and MLB teams, directly involving his office in cultural disputes that are typically outside the purview of the executive branch [3].

### 6.1 Polling Data and Public Sentiment Analysis
Recent polling reveals significant public disapproval of the administration's handling of key domestic issues, indicating potential political vulnerabilities. In another sign of trouble on a signature issue, a separate poll indicates that the President's approval rating on immigration has slipped [2]. The discontent is not limited to the executive branch; polling also claims that Republican Senator Susan Collins's approval rating in her state has reached a record low [3].

Partisan friction is high and affecting policy debates.
